Prophethood
beginner
5 min
Prophetic Attributes: Obligatory, Impossible, and Permissible
Sanusi enumerates three categories of prophetic attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational categories of prophetic attributes and how they are defined.

Core Idea
Prophets must be truthful, trustworthy, and convey the message; their opposites are impossible.

Before examining the proofs, Sanusi first lays out the fundamental attributes that are obligatory, impossible, and permissible for prophets. This classification forms the basis for all later arguments about prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage listing attributes
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify the three categories: obligatory, impossible, and permissible attributes.
The passage begins with 'وأما الرسل' and ends with 'كالمَرَضِ ونَحْوِهِ'.
2
Notice the three obligatory attributes
Truthfulness (sidq), trustworthiness (amana), and conveying (tabligh). Understand why each is essential for a prophet's mission.
3
Identify their opposites as impossible
Lying, betrayal (by committing forbidden or disliked acts), and concealment of the message are impossible for prophets.
Betrayal includes both haram and makruh acts.
4
Understand permissible human attributes
Human conditions like illness are permissible as long as they do not diminish the prophet's high rank.
This opens the door for empirical observation as a proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا الرُّسُلُ عَليهِمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ فَيَجِبُ في حقهم: الصّدقُ، والأمَانَةُ، وتبليغ مَا أُمِرُوا بِتَبْلِيغِهِ للخَلْقِ.
وَيَستَحيلُ فِي حقهم عَليْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ أَضدَادُ هذِهِ الصَّفاتِ، وَهِيَ : الكَذِبُ والخِيانَةَ بفِعْلِ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا نُهُوا عنه نَهْيَ تَخْرِيمٍ أَوْ كَرَاهَةٍ، أَوْ كتمانُ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا أُمِرُوا بِتَبْلِيغِهِ لِلخَلْقِ.
وَيَجُوزُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَليهِمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ مَا هُوَ مِنَ الْأَعْراضِ البَشَرِيَّةِ الَّتِي لَا تُؤَدِّي إِلَى نَقْصٍ فِي مَرَاتِبِهِمُ الْعَلِيَّةِ كَالْمَرَضِ وَنَحْوِهِ. أَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمْ عَليْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ: فَلِأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ لَمْ يَصْدُقُوا لَلزِمَ الْكَذِبُ فِي خَبَرِهِ تَعَالَى، لِتَصْدِيقِهِ تَعَالَى لَهُمْ بِالْمُعْجِزَةِ النَّازِلَةِ مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: صَدَقَ عَبْدِي فِي كُلِّ مَا يُبَلِّغُ عَنِّي.
وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الْأَمَانَةِ لَهُمْ عَليْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ: فَلِأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ خَانُوا بِفِعْلٍ مُحَرَّمٍ أَوْ مَكْرُوهٍ لَانْقَلَبَ الْمُحَرَّمُ أَوِ الْمَكْرُوهُ طَاعَةً فِي حَقِّهِمْ؛ لِأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى أَمَرَنَا بِالاقْتِدَاءِ بِهِمْ فِي أَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ، وَلَا يَأْمُرُ تَعَالَى بِمُحَرَّمٍ وَلَا مَكْرُوهٍ، وَهَذَا بِعَيْنِهِ هُوَ بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الثَّالِثِ.
وَأَمَّا دَلِيلُ جَوَازِ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ: فَمُشَاهَدَةُ وُقُوعِهَا بِهِمْ، إِمَّا لِتَعْظِيمِ أُجُورِهِمْ، أَوْ لِلتَّشْرِيعِ، أَوْ لِلتَّسَلِّي عَنِ الدُّنْيَا، وَالتَّنْبِيهِ لِخِسَّةِالدني
As for the messengers, upon them prayers and peace, it is obligatory in their regard: truthfulness (sidq), trustworthiness (amana), and conveying what they were commanded to convey to creation. And it is impossible in their regard, upon them prayers and peace, the opposites of these attributes, which are: lying, and betraying by doing something of what they were forbidden—either prohibitively or disfavored—and concealing something of what they were commanded to convey to creation. And it is permissible in their regard, upon them prayers and peace, what is from the human attributes that do not lead to a deficiency in their lofty ranks, such as illness and the like. As for the proof of the obligation of their truthfulness, upon them prayers and peace: because if they were not truthful, falsehood would follow in the report of God, Most High, due to His confirming them with the miracle which holds the status of His saying, Most High: 'My servant has spoken truthfully in all that he conveys from Me.' As for the proof of the obligation of trustworthiness for them, upon them prayers and peace: because if they betrayed by a forbidden or disliked act, the forbidden or disliked would turn into obedience in their regard; because God, Most High, commanded us to follow them in their sayings and actions, and He does not command what is forbidden or disliked. And this is exactly the proof for the obligation of the third (attribute). As for the proof of the permissibility of human attributes upon them: it is the observation of their occurrence among them, either to magnify their rewards, or for legislation, or for consolation from the world, and to draw attention to the baseness of the world.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage covers the attributes necessary for prophets, those impossible for them, and those permissible, along with proofs. First, it states that three attributes are wajib (obligatory) for messengers: sidq (truthfulness), amana (trustworthiness), and tabligh (conveying the message). Second, their opposites are mustahil (impossible): lying, betraying by committing forbidden or disliked acts, and concealing any part of the message. Third, it states that human conditions like illness are ja'iz (permissible) as long as they do not lower their high status. Then the proof for sidq: if prophets were not truthful, God would be lying by confirming them through miracles, which is impossible. The proof for amana (and by extension tabligh) is that if they committed forbidden or disliked acts, those acts would become obedience because God commands us to follow them; but God does not command what is forbidden or disliked. Therefore, they must be trustworthy in avoiding such acts and in conveying the message. Finally, the proof for permissibility of human attributes is empirical: we observe them suffering illnesses etc., which either increases their reward, serves as legal precedent, or consoles them from worldly concerns and highlights the world's lowliness.

Key Terms
رسل
صدق
أمانة
تبليغ
كذب
خيانة
كتمان
أعراض بشرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT among the obligatory attributes of prophets according to Sanusi?
A) Truthfulness (sidq)
B) Trustworthiness (amana)
C) Conveying the message (tabligh)
D) Infallibility from human conditions

Key Takeaway
Three categories frame prophetic attributes: obligatory (truthfulness, trustworthiness, conveying), impossible (their opposites), and permissible (non-diminishing human traits).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How do you treat truthfulness in your own life when it is difficult? The prophets were obligated to be truthful always. Where are you tempted to lie in small matters, and what will you commit to changing today?
?
The prophets were entrusted with the greatest message and delivered it without concealment. Do you fully trust in their message, or do you harbor doubts about any part? Take one doubt and resolve to seek knowledge to remove it.
?
Prophets were allowed human weaknesses like illness. Do you accept their humanity, or do you put them on a pedestal beyond your reach? How does acknowledging their humanity affect your connection to them? This week, reflect on one prophet's human struggle and how it inspires you to persevere.

Prophethood
beginner
6 min
Proof of Prophetic Truthfulness and Trustworthiness
Sanusi gives proofs for truthfulness and trustworthiness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proofs for why prophets must be truthful and trustworthy (including conveying the message).

Core Idea
If prophets could lie or betray, God's confirmation through miracles would be false.

After listing the attributes, Sanusi now provides the rational demonstrations. He first proves that truthfulness is necessary by linking it to the miracle that confirms their message, then proves trustworthiness (and by extension conveying) through the divine command to follow them.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof for truthfulness
The proof uses a conditional: if prophets could lie, then God would be lying by confirming them with miracles.
The miracle is like God saying 'My servant has spoken truthfully.'
2
Understand the role of miracles
Miracles are signs from God that the prophet is truthful. If the prophet were lying, the miracle would be endorsing a lie, which is impossible for God.
3
Read the proof for trustworthiness (and tabligh)
God commands us to follow the prophets. If they committed forbidden or disliked acts, those acts would become obedience, which is contradictory.
This same proof covers the obligation to convey the message, as failure to convey would be a betrayal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا الرُّسُلُ عَليهِمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ فَيَجِبُ في حقهم: الصّدقُ، والأمَانَةُ، وتبليغ مَا أُمِرُوا بِتَبْلِيغِهِ للخَلْقِ.
وَيَستَحيلُ فِي حقهم عَليْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ أَضدَادُ هذِهِ الصَّفاتِ، وَهِيَ : الكَذِبُ والخِيانَةَ بفِعْلِ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا نُهُوا عنه نَهْيَ تَخْرِيمٍ أَوْ كَرَاهَةٍ، أَوْ كتمانُ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا أُمِرُوا بِتَبْلِيغِهِ لِلخَلْقِ.
وَيَجُوزُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَليهِمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ مَا هُوَ مِنَ الْأَعْراضِ البَشَرِيَّةِ الَّتِي لَا تُؤَدِّي إِلَى نَقْصٍ فِي مَرَاتِبِهِمُ الْعَلِيَّةِ كَالْمَرَضِ وَنَحْوِهِ. أَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمْ عَليْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ: فَلِأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ لَمْ يَصْدُقُوا لَلزِمَ الْكَذِبُ فِي خَبَرِهِ تَعَالَى، لِتَصْدِيقِهِ تَعَالَى لَهُمْ بِالْمُعْجِزَةِ النَّازِلَةِ مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: صَدَقَ عَبْدِي فِي كُلِّ مَا يُبَلِّغُ عَنِّي.
وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الْأَمَانَةِ لَهُمْ عَليْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ: فَلِأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ خَانُوا بِفِعْلٍ مُحَرَّمٍ أَوْ مَكْرُوهٍ لَانْقَلَبَ الْمُحَرَّمُ أَوِ الْمَكْرُوهُ طَاعَةً فِي حَقِّهِمْ؛ لِأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى أَمَرَنَا بِالاقْتِدَاءِ بِهِمْ فِي أَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ، وَلَا يَأْمُرُ تَعَالَى بِمُحَرَّمٍ وَلَا مَكْرُوهٍ، وَهَذَا بِعَيْنِهِ هُوَ بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الثَّالِثِ.
وَأَمَّا دَلِيلُ جَوَازِ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ: فَمُشَاهَدَةُ وُقُوعِهَا بِهِمْ، إِمَّا لِتَعْظِيمِ أُجُورِهِمْ، أَوْ لِلتَّشْرِيعِ، أَوْ لِلتَّسَلِّي عَنِ الدُّنْيَا، وَالتَّنْبِيهِ لِخِسَّةِالدني
As for the messengers, upon them prayers and peace, it is obligatory in their regard: truthfulness (sidq), trustworthiness (amana), and conveying what they were commanded to convey to creation. And it is impossible in their regard, upon them prayers and peace, the opposites of these attributes, which are: lying, and betraying by doing something of what they were forbidden—either prohibitively or disfavored—and concealing something of what they were commanded to convey to creation. And it is permissible in their regard, upon them prayers and peace, what is from the human attributes that do not lead to a deficiency in their lofty ranks, such as illness and the like. As for the proof of the obligation of their truthfulness, upon them prayers and peace: because if they were not truthful, falsehood would follow in the report of God, Most High, due to His confirming them with the miracle which holds the status of His saying, Most High: 'My servant has spoken truthfully in all that he conveys from Me.' As for the proof of the obligation of trustworthiness for them, upon them prayers and peace: because if they betrayed by a forbidden or disliked act, the forbidden or disliked would turn into obedience in their regard; because God, Most High, commanded us to follow them in their sayings and actions, and He does not command what is forbidden or disliked. And this is exactly the proof for the obligation of the third (attribute). As for the proof of the permissibility of human attributes upon them: it is the observation of their occurrence among them, either to magnify their rewards, or for legislation, or for consolation from the world, and to draw attention to the baseness of the world.

Commentary
This passage covers the attributes necessary for prophets, those impossible for them, and those permissible, along with proofs. First, it states that three attributes are wajib (obligatory) for messengers: sidq (truthfulness), amana (trustworthiness), and tabligh (conveying the message). Second, their opposites are mustahil (impossible): lying, betraying by committing forbidden or disliked acts, and concealing any part of the message. Third, it states that human conditions like illness are ja'iz (permissible) as long as they do not lower their high status. Then the proof for sidq: if prophets were not truthful, God would be lying by confirming them through miracles, which is impossible. The proof for amana (and by extension tabligh) is that if they committed forbidden or disliked acts, those acts would become obedience because God commands us to follow them; but God does not command what is forbidden or disliked. خيانة
معجزة
الاقتداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophethood can be proven without miracles.
Correction: Sanusi's proof shows that miracles are essential because they serve as God's endorsement of the prophet's truthfulness.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what would necessarily follow if prophets were not truthful?
A) People would not believe them.
B) God's report would be false.
C) They would not perform miracles.
D) Their teachings would be inconsistent.

Key Takeaway
Truthfulness is proven by miracles; trustworthiness is proven by the command to follow prophets, which cannot include forbidden acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that every word of the Prophet (peace be upon him) is truthful because God confirms it, why do you sometimes hesitate to act on his teachings when they contradict your desires?
?
Reflect on a time you chose to follow a cultural norm over a prophetic teaching. How does the proof that prophets cannot betray God's message challenge that choice?
?
The proof of trustworthiness means the Prophet never did anything God disapproves of. How does that understanding change your view of his actions that you previously found difficult to accept?

Prophethood
beginner
4 min
Proof of Permissible Human Attributes for Prophets
Sanusti justifies permissible prophetic attributes empirically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why human conditions like illness are permissible for prophets and what purposes they serve.

Core Idea
Observing prophets with human attributes proves they are permissible, and these trials have wisdom.

The final proof addresses the permissible category. Unlike the previous proofs that are rational, this proof is empirical: we simply see prophets experiencing human conditions. Sanusi also explains the wisdom behind these occurrences.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof for permissible attributes
The proof is based on observation: we see prophets falling ill and experiencing other human conditions.
This is called 'mushahada' (observation/direct experience).
2
Understand the three wisdoms
These conditions happen to increase rewards, to establish legal precedents, or to console prophets from worldly attachments.
The Arabic mentions three purposes: تعظيم أجورهم, للتشريع, للتسلي عن الدنيا.
3
Reflect on the baseness of this world
The final purpose mentioned is to draw attention to the lowliness of the world, so prophets are not attached to it.
The passage cuts off at 'التنبيه لخسة الدني' likely meaning 'الدنيا'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا الرُّسُلُ عَليهِمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ فَيَجِبُ في حقهم: الصّدقُ، والأمَانَةُ، وتبليغ مَا أُمِرُوا بِتَبْلِيغِهِ للخَلْقِ.
وَيَستَحيلُ فِي حقهم عَليْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ أَضدَادُ هذِهِ الصَّفاتِ، وَهِيَ : الكَذِبُ والخِيانَةَ بفِعْلِ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا نُهُوا عنه نَهْيَ تَخْرِيمٍ أَوْ كَرَاهَةٍ، أَوْ كتمانُ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا أُمِرُوا بِتَبْلِيغِهِ لِلخَلْقِ.
وَيَجُوزُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَليهِمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ مَا هُوَ مِنَ الْأَعْراضِ البَشَرِيَّةِ الَّتِي لَا تُؤَدِّي إِلَى نَقْصٍ فِي مَرَاتِبِهِمُ الْعَلِيَّةِ كَالْمَرَضِ وَنَحْوِهِ. أَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمْ عَليْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ: فَلِأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ لَمْ يَصْدُقُوا لَلزِمَ الْكَذِبُ فِي خَبَرِهِ تَعَالَى، لِتَصْدِيقِهِ تَعَالَى لَهُمْ بِالْمُعْجِزَةِ النَّازِلَةِ مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: صَدَقَ عَبْدِي فِي كُلِّ مَا يُبَلِّغُ عَنِّي.
وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الْأَمَانَةِ لَهُمْ عَليْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ: فَلِأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ خَانُوا بِفِعْلٍ مُحَرَّمٍ أَوْ مَكْرُوهٍ لَانْقَلَبَ الْمُحَرَّمُ أَوِ الْمَكْرُوهُ طَاعَةً فِي حَقِّهِمْ؛ لِأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى أَمَرَنَا بِالاقْتِدَاءِ بِهِمْ فِي أَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ، وَلَا يَأْمُرُ تَعَالَى بِمُحَرَّمٍ وَلَا مَكْرُوهٍ، وَهَذَا بِعَيْنِهِ هُوَ بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الثَّالِثِ.
وَأَمَّا دَلِيلُ جَوَازِ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ: فَمُشَاهَدَةُ وُقُوعِهَا بِهِمْ، إِمَّا لِتَعْظِيمِ أُجُورِهِمْ، أَوْ لِلتَّشْرِيعِ، أَوْ لِلتَّسَلِّي عَنِ الدُّنْيَا، وَالتَّنْبِيهِ لِخِسَّةِالدني
As for the messengers, upon them prayers and peace, it is obligatory in their regard: truthfulness (sidq), trustworthiness (amana), and conveying what they were commanded to convey to creation. And it is impossible in their regard, upon them prayers and peace, the opposites of these attributes, which are: lying, and betraying by doing something of what they were forbidden—either prohibitively or disfavored—and concealing something of what they were commanded to convey to creation. And it is permissible in their regard, upon them prayers and peace, what is from the human attributes that do not lead to a deficiency in their lofty ranks, such as illness and the like. As for the proof of the obligation of their truthfulness, upon them prayers and peace: because if they were not truthful, falsehood would follow in the report of God, Most High, due to His confirming them with the miracle which holds the status of His saying, Most High: 'My servant has spoken truthfully in all that he conveys from Me.' As for the proof of the obligation of trustworthiness for them, upon them prayers and peace: because if they betrayed by a forbidden or disliked act, the forbidden or disliked would turn into obedience in their regard; because God, Most High, commanded us to follow them in their sayings and actions, and He does not command what is forbidden or disliked. And this is exactly the proof for the obligation of the third (attribute). As for the proof of the permissibility of human attributes upon them: it is the observation of their occurrence among them, either to magnify their rewards, or for legislation, or for consolation from the world, and to draw attention to the baseness of the world.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage covers the attributes necessary for prophets, those impossible for them, and those permissible, along with proofs. First, it states that three attributes are wajib (obligatory) for messengers: sidq (truthfulness), amana (trustworthiness), and tabligh (conveying the message). Second, their opposites are mustahil (impossible): lying, betraying by committing forbidden or disliked acts, and concealing any part of the message. Third, it states that human conditions like illness are ja'iz (permissible) as long as they do not lower their high status. Then the proof for sidq: if prophets were not truthful, God would be lying by confirming them through miracles, which is impossible. The proof for amana (and by extension tabligh) is that if they committed forbidden or disliked acts, those acts would become obedience because God commands us to follow them; but God does not command what is forbidden or disliked. Therefore, they must be trustworthy in avoiding such acts and in conveying the message. Finally, the proof for permissibility of human attributes is empirical: we observe them suffering illnesses etc., which either increases their reward, serves as legal precedent, or consoles them from worldly concerns and highlights the world's lowliness.

Key Terms
أعراض بشرية
مشاهدة
تعظيم أجور
تشريع
تسلي
خسة الدنيا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that any human condition is impossible for prophets because they are perfect.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that only conditions that lower their rank are impossible; others like illness are permissible and even beneficial.

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof for the permissibility of human attributes like illness for prophets?
A) Rational deduction from God's justice.
B) Observation that such events occurred with prophets.
C) Consensus of scholars.
D) Scriptural texts.

Key Takeaway
Human attributes like illness are permissible for prophets; they serve wise purposes such as increasing reward, legislating, and reminding of the world's lowliness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial or hardship, do you genuinely believe it could be a means to increase your reward, or do you see it only as a punishment? What would it take for you to change that perspective today?
?
The prophets' trials served to teach the community. Your personal trials—are you learning from them, or are you merely enduring them without seeking the wisdom behind them?
?
If you truly internalized that this world is base and lowly, what specific attachment in your life would you begin to loosen? What step will you take today to remind yourself of its worthlessness?

The Three Categories of Prophetic Attributes
Sanusi enumerates the wajib, mustahil, and ja'iz attributes of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational categories of prophetic attributes: necessary, impossible, and possible, and their specific examples.

Core Idea
Prophets must be truthful, trustworthy, and deliver the message; their opposites are impossible.

Sanusi now turns from the attributes of Allah to the attributes of prophets. Just as Allah has necessary, impossible, and possible attributes, so do the messengers. This passage establishes the core prophetic qualities that define their mission and character. Read carefully to see how each category is defined and what it entails.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage aloud
Read the Arabic text slowly, noticing the three key verbs: يجب, يستحيل, يجوز. These structure the entire passage.
The passage is concise but packed with doctrinal content.
2
Identify the three categories
Find the three rational judgments (wajib, mustahil, ja'iz) and note the specific attributes listed under each.
3
Understand the opposites
The mustahil attributes are the direct opposites of the wajib ones. See how Sanusi defines betrayal (khiyana) as doing what is forbidden or disliked, and concealing the message.
The phrase 'نهي تخريم' is likely 'نهي تحريم' (prohibition of forbiddance) – a minor OCR issue.
4
Consider the ja'iz category
The ja'iz attributes are human traits that do not diminish the prophet's rank. Reflect on why illness is permissible but sin is not.
This shows prophets are human but protected from sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا الرُّسُلُ عَليهِمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ فَيَجِبُ في حقهم: الصّدقُ، والأمَانَةُ، وتبليغ مَا أُمِرُوا بِتَبْلِيغِهِ للخَلْقِ. وَيَستَحيلُ فِي حقهم عَليْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ أَضدَادُ هذِهِ الصَّفاتِ، وَهِيَ : الكَذِبُ والخِيانَةَ بفِعْلِ شيءٍ مِمَّا نُهُوا عنه نهي تخريم أَوْ كَرَاهِةٍ، أَوْ كتمانُ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا أُمِرُوا بِتِبْلِيغِهِ لِلخَلْقِ. وَيَجُوزُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَليهِمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ مَا هُوَ مِنَ الْأَعْراضِ البشريَّةِ التي لا تُؤَدّي إلى نَقْصٍ في مَراتِبهِم العَليَّةِ كالمَرَضِ وَنحوِهِ.
As for the messengers, upon them prayers and peace, there is required (wajib) in their right: truthfulness, trustworthiness, and delivering what they were commanded to deliver to the creation. And it is impossible (mustahil) in their right, upon them prayers and peace, the opposites of these attributes, which are: lying, betrayal by doing something of what they were forbidden from by a prohibition of prohibition or a prohibition of dislike, or concealing something of what they were commanded to deliver to the creation. And it is permissible (ja'iz) in their right, upon them prayers and peace, what is from human accidents (a'rad bashariyya) that do not lead to a deficiency in their lofty ranks, such as illness and the like.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage classifies the attributes of prophets into three rational categories: wajib (necessary), mustahil (impossible), and ja'iz (possible). The wajib attributes are three: truthfulness (sidq), trustworthiness (amana), and delivering the message (tabligh). Their opposites – lying, betrayal (by doing what is forbidden or disliked), and concealing the message – are mustahil. Finally, human accidents (a'rad bashariyya) that do not diminish their high rank, such as illness, are ja'iz for them. This establishes the normative framework for prophetic attributes.

Misconception: Some think prophets cannot experience any human attributes like illness.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly states that human accidents (a'rad bashariyya) that do not cause deficiency in their rank, such as illness, are permissible for prophets.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Prophets must be truthful, trustworthy, and deliver the message; their opposites are impossible, while non-diminishing human traits are permissible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) was required to be truthful in all matters. When you speak, do you mirror that same truthfulness, even when it costs you? Think of a situation today where you were less than truthful. What will you change tomorrow?
?
The attribute of tabligh means the Prophet concealed nothing of the message. Do you feel any impatience or selective attention when listening to parts of the Quran or hadith that challenge your lifestyle? How will you strive to receive the entire message with submission?
?
Prophets cannot even commit disliked actions. How does this standard affect your view of the 'minor' sins or disliked habits in your own life? Are you treating them lightly? What step can you take today to avoid even a makruh action out of love for your Prophet?

Rational Proofs for Prophetic Attributes
Sanusi provides rational proofs for three prophetic attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proofs that establish truthfulness, trustworthiness, and delivery as necessary attributes of prophets.

Core Idea
A prophet's truthfulness is proven by the miracle; trustworthiness and delivery follow from our duty to emulate them.

Sanusi now turns from defining the necessary attributes of prophets to proving them. He presents three concise rational arguments, each built on a single premise. The first uses miracles as divine confirmation, the second and third use the fact that Allah commands us to emulate the prophets in all their words and actions. This passage shows how each proof works.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Notice how each proof is introduced with 'أما برهان...'.
The passage is structured as two explicit proofs, with a note that the third is the same as the second.
2
Understand the proof for truthfulness
Focus on the logic: if a prophet could lie, then Allah's confirmation by miracle would be false, implying falsehood in Allah's report. A miracle is like Allah saying 'My servant is truthful.'
This is a rational argument, not just a textual one.
3
Understand the proof for trustworthiness and delivery
If a prophet committed a forbidden or disliked act, then because Allah commands us to follow them, that act would become an act of obedience, which is impossible. The same logic applies to concealing the message.
The third attribute (tabligh) is proven by the same reasoning, as concealing would be a form of betrayal.
4
Reflect on the rational nature of these proofs
Ask yourself why these proofs are considered rational (burhan) rather than based solely on scripture. They rely on logical consequences of the role of prophets.
This connects to the broader method of Ilm al-Kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمَّا بُرْهانُ وُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمْ عَليْهِمُ الصلاةُ والسَّلامُ : فلِأَنَّهُمْ لَو لمْ يَصْدُقُوا للزمَ الكَذِبُ في خَبَرِهِ تَعالى، لِتَصْدِيقِه تَعَالى لَهُم بِالمُعْجِزَةِ النَّازِلَة مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ تعالى: صَدَقَ عَبْدِي فِي كُلِّ مَا يُبَلِّغُ عَنِّي. وأمَّا بُرْهانُ وُجُوبِ الأمَانَةِ لهُم عَليْهم الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ: فَلِأَنَّهُمْ لَو خَانُوا بِفعل مُحرَّم ا مَكروه لاتقلبَ المُحَرَّمُ أَوِ المَكرُوهُ طَاعَةٌ في حَقِّهِمْ؛ لأنَّ الله تَعَالى أَمَرنَا بالاقتدَاءِ بهم في أقوالهم وأفعالِهِمْ، وَلا يَأْمُرُ تَعالى بِمُحرَّم ولا مكرُوهِ، وَهَذا بِعيْنهِ هُوَ بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الثَّالِثِ.
As for the proof of the necessity of their truthfulness, upon them prayers and peace: because if they were not truthful, then falsehood would be necessary in His report, exalted is He, due to His affirming them by the miracle which is in the position of His saying: 'My servant has spoken truthfully in everything he conveys from Me.' And as for the proof of the necessity of trustworthiness for them, upon them prayers and peace: because if they were to betray by doing a forbidden or disliked act, then the forbidden or disliked would turn into an act of obedience in their right; because Allah, exalted is He, commanded us to follow them in their statements and actions, and He, exalted, does not command a forbidden or disliked act. And this itself is the proof of the necessity of the third (attribute).
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage presents the rational proofs (burhan) for why the three wajib attributes of prophets are necessary. The proof for truthfulness: if prophets could lie, then Allah's confirmation of their truth by performing miracles would itself be a lie, because the miracle serves as Allah's statement that the prophet is truthful. The proof for trustworthiness: if a prophet committed a forbidden or disliked act, then because Allah commands us to follow them in all they do, that act would become an act of obedience (ta'a) in their case. But Allah does not command what is forbidden or disliked, so such acts cannot occur from them. The same proof applies to the third attribute, tabligh, because concealing the message would be a form of betrayal.

Key Terms
برهان
صدق
أمانة
تبليغ
معجزة
اقتداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the proof for truthfulness relies solely on miracles as external signs, not as a rational argument.
Correction: The miracle is positioned as Allah's statement confirming the prophet, making it a rational necessity: if the prophet lied, Allah's statement would be false, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if a prophet were to lie, according to Sanusi's proof?
A) The miracle would still confirm him.
B) Allah's report would be false.
C) The prophet would be punished.
D) The people would not follow him.

Key Takeaway
The necessity of prophetic attributes is rationally proven: miracles confirm truthfulness, and the command to emulate them guarantees trustworthiness and delivery.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If a miracle is God's declaration that the Prophet (saw) is absolutely truthful in everything he conveys, then how do you treat his reports about the unseen, the afterlife, and moral commands in your daily decisions? Where do you fall short in acting on them as absolute truth?
?
The proof for trustworthiness shows that the Prophet (saw) could not have committed even a disliked act because Allah commands you to emulate him. What single habit or action in your life does not align with the sunnah, and what is the first step you will take today to change it?
?
Given that delivery of the message is a necessary attribute, the Prophet (saw) did not conceal any part of the guidance. Are there any parts of that guidance that you find yourself ignoring or downplaying because they are inconvenient? Will you commit to studying and implementing them starting this week?

Proof of Permissible Human Ailments for Prophets
Sanusi proves the permissibility of human ailments for prophets by citing observed examples and enumerating divine wisdoms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proof for why prophets can experience human ailments and the four divine wisdoms behind their occurrence.

Core Idea
Prophets' human ailments are permissible, observed in history, and serve profound divine purposes.

Sanusi now addresses a key objection: if prophets are the best of creation, why do they suffer from illness and hardship? The answer lies not in denying these occurrences but in understanding their purpose. The proof is simple—we observe them—and the wisdom behind them is manifold, from elevating rewards to teaching reliance on Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully. Notice that Sanusi begins with the proof (dalil) itself, then lists four purposes.
The proof is observation (mushahada), not rational argument.
2
Identify the four purposes
List the four reasons given for why prophets experience human ailments: (1) to magnify rewards, (2) for legislation, (3) for consolation from the world, (4) to show the lowliness of this world.
These purposes are not random; they are all beneficial for the prophet and the community.
3
Reflect on the phrase 'dar jazaa'
Notice the final phrase about this world not being an abode of recompense for prophets and saints. This teaches that the true reward is in the Hereafter.
4
Connect to lesson's big picture
Consider how this proof fits into the overall argument for prophethood and defends prophets from having to be insulated from all human experiences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا دَلِيلُ جَوَازِ الأعرَاضِ البشريَّةِ عَليْهم: فَمُشاهَدَةُ وُقُوعها بِهِمْ، إما لتعظيم أُجُورِهِمْ، أو للتشريع، أوْ لِلتَّسَلِّي عَن الدُّنْيَا، وَالتَّنْبِيهِ لخِسَّةِ قَدْرِهَا عِنْدَ اللهِ تَعَالَى، وَعَدمِ رِضَاهُ تَعَالَى بِهَا دَارَ جزاء لأَنْبِيَائِهِ وأَوْلِيَائِهِ بِاعْتِبَارِ أحْوَالِهِمْ فيها عَليْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ .
And as for the proof of the permissibility of human accidents (a'rad bashariyya) upon them: it is the observation of their occurrence with them, either to magnify their rewards, or for legislation (tashri'), or for consolation from this world, and to alert to the lowliness of its worth with Allah, exalted is He, and His lack of satisfaction with it as an abode of recompense for His prophets and friends (awliya') with consideration of their states in it, upon them prayers and peace.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage provides the proof (dalil) for why human attributes (a'rad bashariyya) such as illness are permissible for prophets. The proof is based on observation (mushahada): we actually see these attributes occurring with prophets. Moreover, their occurrence serves wise purposes: (1) to increase their rewards by enduring hardships, (2) for legislation (tashri') by showing how to handle such situations, (3) to provide consolation for this world, and (4) to alert people to the lowliness of this world and that Allah is not pleased with it as a reward for His prophets and saints.

أعراض بشرية
مشاهدة
تعظيم أجور
تشريع
تسلي
تنبيه

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets must be completely free from all human limitations and ailments to maintain their status.
Correction: This passage shows that human ailments are permissible for prophets and actually serve divine purposes, thus not diminishing their rank.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the primary proof for the permissibility of human ailments upon prophets?
A) Rational deduction
B) Observation of their occurrence
C) Consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
Prophets can experience human ailments because we observe them, and these occurrences carry deep wisdom: magnifying rewards, providing legislation, offering consolation, and showing the lowliness of this world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

What would change if you truly believed that Allah does not intend this world as a place of reward for His beloved ones?

Deriving Prophetic Attributes from the Second Shahada
Sanusi derives prophetic attributes and required beliefs from the second shahada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the second shahada logically implies belief in all previous prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day, as well as the necessity of prophetic truthfulness, the impossibility of lying and sin, and the permissibility of human attributes for prophets.

Core Idea
The second shahada is a compact creed that unfolds into a framework of prophetic attributes.

Sanusi uses the second shahada as a cornerstone to deduce essential beliefs about prophethood. In this passage, he shows that affirming Muhammad as a messenger logically commits us to affirming all messengers, the angels, scriptures, and the Hereafter, and also establishes the prophets' truthfulness, infallibility from sin, and the permissibility of normal human experiences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally.
2
Identify the four entailments
From the shahada, Sanusi derives four things: belief in all prophets/angels/books/Last Day, necessity of truthfulness, impossibility of sin, permissibility of human attributes.
List them in order as they appear.
3
Examine the logical reasoning
For each entailment, note why it follows. For example, truthfulness is necessary because a liar cannot be a trustworthy messenger. Prohibited acts are impossible because prophets teach by example.
4
Reflect on the human attributes misconception
The passage clarifies that human attributes like illness or poverty do not diminish prophethood; they increase merit.
This is a common misunderstanding corrected by Sanusi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا قَوْلُنَا: مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَعَلَى آلِهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ: الإِيمَانُ بِسَائِرِ الأَنْبِيَاءِ وَالْمَلائِكَةِ وَالْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ وَالْيَوْمِ الآخِرِ؛ لأَنَّهُ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَعَلَى آلِهِ وَسَلَّمَ جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ. وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ: وُجُوبُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ، وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الْكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وإِلَّا لَمْ يَكُونُوا رُسُلاً أُمَنَاءَ لِمَوْلانَا الْعَالِمِ بِالْخَفِيَّاتِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ. وَاسْتِحَالَةُ فِعْلِ الْمَنْهِيَّاتِ كُلِّهَا؛ لأَنَّهُمْ أُرْسِلُوا لِيُعَلِّمُوا الْخَلْقَ بِأَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ وَسُكُوتِهِمْ. فَيَلْزَمُ أَنْ لا يَكُونَ فِي جَمِيعِهَا مُخَالَفَةٌ لأَمْرِ مَوْلانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الَّذِي اخْتَارَهُمْ عَلَى جَمِيعِ الْخَلْقِ، وَأَمَّنَهُمْ عَلَى سِرِّ وَحْيِهِ. وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ: جَوَازُ الأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمُ؛ إِذْ ذَاكَ لا يَقْدَحُ فِي رِسَالَتِهِمْ وَعُلُوِّ مَنْزِلَتِهِمْ عِنْدَ اللهِ تَعَالَى، بَلْ ذَاكَ مِمَّا يَزِيدُ فِيهَا.
And as for our statement: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of God, may God bless him and his family and grant them peace,' it includes: faith in all the prophets, angels, heavenly books, and the Last Day; because he, may God bless him and his family and grant him peace, came with the affirmation of all of that. And from it is derived: the necessity of truthfulness of the messengers, prayers and peace be upon them, and the impossibility of lying upon them; otherwise they would not be trustworthy messengers for our Master, the Knower of hidden things, Majestic and Mighty. And the impossibility of committing all prohibited acts; because they were sent to teach creation by their words, actions, and silences. So it necessarily follows that there should be in all of that no opposition to the command of our Master, Majestic and Mighty, who chose them over all creation and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation. And from it is derived: the permissibility of human accidents upon them; for that does not detract from their message and the highness of their station with Allah, exalted, rather that is something that increases it.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition of the second shahada (Muhammadun Rasul Allah). Sanusi shows that this declaration logically entails several beliefs and prophetic attributes. First, it requires belief in all prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day, because the Prophet came confirming all of them. Second, from the shahada we derive the necessity (wujub) of truthfulness for prophets and the impossibility (istihala) of lying, since they are entrusted with God's revelation—a liar cannot be an amana (trustworthy). Third, it entails the impossibility of committing any forbidden acts (manhiyyat), because prophets are teachers by word, deed, and silence; any disobedience would contradict their teaching mission. Fourth, it permits (jawaz) human accidents (a'rad bashariyya) such as illness or poverty, as these do not impair their prophetic status but rather increase their merit. The passage follows a logical order: from the fact of prophethood, necessary attributes (truthfulness, infallibility) and permissible human traits are deduced.

Key Terms
الرسل
الصدق
استحالة الكذب
المنهيات
الأعراض البشرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human attributes (like eating, sleeping, illness) contradict prophethood or lower a prophet's status.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that such attributes are permissible and do not detract from their message; rather, they increase their merit.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is it impossible for prophets to commit prohibited acts?
A) Because they are sinless by nature
B) Because they are sent to teach by their words, actions, and silences
C) Because they are angels in human form
D) Because God prevents them from any sin by force

Key Takeaway
The second shahada is a foundation for a comprehensive belief system about prophethood, requiring faith in all messengers, affirming their truthfulness and sinlessness, and allowing their human experiences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
Human weaknesses like illness or poverty did not diminish the prophets' rank. Why do you often feel ashamed of your own limitations? What would it look like to turn your greatest weakness into a means of drawing closer to Allah?

Implications of the Shahada Regarding the Prophets and Its Comprehensiveness
Sanusi deduces necessary beliefs about prophets from the shahada and explains its comprehensiveness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three essential beliefs about the prophets derived from the shahada and why the shahada is considered comprehensive.

Core Idea
The shahada implies that prophets must be truthful, sinless, and human.

The testimony of faith, 'La ilaha illa Allah, Muhammadun rasul Allah,' is the foundation of Islam. But what does it entail beyond affirming God's oneness and Muhammad's prophethood? In this passage, Imam al-Sanusi extracts profound implications about the nature of prophets and demonstrates how these few words encompass all necessary beliefs. Let's explore how the shahada shapes our understanding of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's flow come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical connectors: 'ويؤخذ منه' (and it is derived from this).
2
Identify the three implications
The passage lists three derived beliefs about prophets: wajib al-sidq (obligation of truthfulness), istihalat al-kidhb (impossibility of lying), istihalat fi'l al-munhiyat (impossibility of prohibited acts), and jawaz al-a'rad al-bashariyya (permissibility of human accidents). Find each one and note the reasoning given.
3
Understand the comprehensiveness argument
Sanusi argues that despite its few words, the shahada contains all necessary beliefs. See how he connects this to the Law's acceptance of faith only through the shahada.
Reflect on why brevity with depth is powerful.
4
Reflect on the practice
The passage ends with an exhortation to frequently recite the shahada with mindfulness. Consider how this lesson calls you to internalize the shahada's meanings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأنبياء والملائكة والكتب السَّماوية واليوم الآخر؛ لأَنَّهُ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَعَلَى آلِهِ وَسَلَّمَ جَاءَ بتصديق جميع ذلك. ويؤخذ منه: وجوب صدق الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام، واستحالة الكذب عليهم، وإلا لم يكونوا رسلاً أمناء لموْلانا العالم بالخفيَّات جلّ وعزّ واستحالة فعل المنهيَّات كلها؛ لأَنَّهُمْ أرسلوا ليُعلِّموا الخلق بأقوالهم وأفعالهم وسكوتهم. فيلزم أن لا يكون في جميعها مخالفة لأمر مَوْلانا جل وعز الذي اختارهم على جميع الخلق، وأمَّنهم على سرّ وحيه. ويؤخذ منه: جواز الأعراض البشرية عليهم؛ إذ ذاك لا يقدح في رسالتهم وعلو منزلتهم عند الله تعالى، بل ذاك مما يزيد فيها. فقد اتضح لك تضمن كلمتي الشهادة مع قلة حروفها لجميع ما يجب على المكلَّف معرفته من عقائد الإيمان في حقه تعالى وفي حق رسله عليهم الصلاة والسلام. ولعلها لاختصارها مع اشتمالها على ما ذكرناه جعلها الشرع ترجمة على ما في القلب من الإسلام، ولم يقبل من أحد الإيمان إلا بها. فعلى العاقل أن يكثر من ذكرها، مستحضراً لما احتوت عليه من عقائد الإيمان، حتى تمتزج مع معناها بلحمه ودمه، فإنه يرى لها من الأسرار والعجائب إن شاء الله تعالى ما لا يدخل تحت حصر. وبالله تعالى التوفيق لا رَبَّ غيره، ولا معبود سواه، نسأله سبحانه أن يجعلنا وأحبَّتنا عند الموت ناطقين بكلمتي الشهادة، عالمين بها. وصلى الله على سيدنا ومولانا محمد كلما ذكره الذاكرون، وغفل عن ذكره الغافلون، ورضي الله عن أصحاب رسول الله أجمعين، وعن التابعين لهم بإحسان إلى يوم الدين، وسلام على المرسلين، والحمد لله رب العالمين.
The prophets, angels, divine books, and the Last Day; because he (SAW) came confirming all of that. And it is derived from this: the obligation of truthfulness of the messengers (upon them peace), and the impossibility of lying upon them, otherwise they would not be trustworthy messengers for our Lord, the Knower of hidden things, Mighty and Majestic; and the impossibility of committing all prohibited acts; because they were sent to teach creation by their words, actions, and silence. So it follows that there should not be in all of them any opposition to the command of our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, who chose them over all creation and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation. And it is derived from this: the permissibility of human accidents for them; for that does not detract from their message and high station with God Most High, rather that increases it. So it has become clear to you that the two words of testimony, despite the fewness of their letters, encompass all that the responsible person must know of the beliefs of faith regarding Him Most High and regarding His messengers (upon them peace). And perhaps because of their brevity while containing what we have mentioned, the Law made them an expression of what is in the heart of Islam, and He did not accept faith from anyone except through them. So it is upon the intelligent person to frequently mention them, being mindful of what they contain of the beliefs of faith, until they mix with their meaning into his flesh and blood, for he will see of them secrets and wonders, if God wills, that cannot be enumerated. And with God Most High is success, there is no lord besides Him, no deity other than Him. We ask Him, exalted, to make us and our loved ones at death utterers of the two words of testimony, knowers of them. And may God bless our master and lord Muhammad, whenever those who remember remember him, and whenever those who neglect neglect his remembrance; and may God be pleased with all the companions of the Messenger of God, and with the followers who followed them in excellence until the Day of Judgment; and peace be upon the messengers, and praise be to God, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion drawn from the testimony of faith (shahada) regarding the prophets and a demonstration of the comprehensiveness of the two testimonies. The author, Imam al-Sanusi, begins by stating that the Prophet Muhammad (SAW) confirmed belief in the prophets, angels, divine books, and the Last Day. From this affirmation, he derives several necessary beliefs about the prophets. First, it obligates that the prophets must be truthful (wujub sidq al-rusul) and that lying is impossible for them (istihalat al-kidhb 'alayhim), for otherwise they would not be trustworthy messengers entrusted by God, who knows all hidden things. Second, it necessitates the impossibility of their committing any prohibited acts (istihalat fi'l al-munhiyat kulliha), because they were sent to teach people by their words, actions, and silence; therefore, none of these should contradict God's command, as God chose them over all creation and entrusted them with His revelation. Third, from this it is derived that human accidents or ordinary human attributes (al-a'rad al-bashariyya) are permissible for them (jawaz), because such things do not impair their message or lofty station; rather, they increase it. The author then emphasizes that the two words of testimony (la ilaha illa Allah, Muhammadun rasul Allah) despite their brevity encompass all that a responsible person (mukallaf) must know of the beliefs of faith concerning God and His messengers. Because of this comprehensiveness, Islamic law made these words the expression of the faith in the heart and does not accept faith from anyone except through them. The author exhorts the intelligent person to frequently recite them while being mindful of their meanings, so that they become ingrained in one's being, leading to spiritual insights beyond enumeration. The passage concludes with prayers for steadfastness in uttering the shahada at death and the traditional blessings upon the Prophet, his companions, and followers.

Correction: The passage clarifies that human accidents are permissible and even increase their station.

Key Takeaway
The shahada alone implies that prophets are truthful, sinless, and possess human attributes, and it summaries all articles of faith.

Basmala's Indirect Indication to Prophethood and Sam'iyyat
Al-Anbabi elucidates the basmala's indirect indication to prophethood and sam'iyyat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the basmala, though not explicitly mentioning prophethood or sam'iyyat, indirectly points to these fundamental creedal matters through the logic of compliance with hadith and the concept of divine blessings.

Core Idea
The basmala hints at prophethood and the unseen through compliance with hadith and blessings.

This passage deepens our appreciation of the basmala by showing that it contains more than just a mention of Allah's attributes—it indirectly signals the proofs of prophethood and the realities of the unseen (sam'iyyat). The author responds to a doubt about this subtle reference, offering a layered argument that ties the simple act of recitation to the deepest creedal foundations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get a sense of the argument. Notice how the author addresses an objection and then provides a clarification.
The passage is from al-Anbabi's commentary.
2
Identify the initial objection
The passage begins with an objection: some say the basmala does not clearly indicate the creeds related to prophets and sam'iyyat. Underline this doubt.
3
Trace the first response: compliance logic
The first response argues that reciting the basmala in compliance with hadith presupposes belief in the truthfulness of the Prophet (narrator). That truthfulness leads to accepting his reports about prophets being infallible and about sam'iyyat.
This is an indirect indication through a chain of reasoning.
4
Examine the second response: blessings
The alternative explanation states that sending prophets supported by miracles is part of Allah's blessings mentioned in the basmala. This is a more direct indication.
The author notes that the criterion is mere indication, not strict entailment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد علمت من هذا: أن فيها أيضاً إشارةً إلى أدلة العقائد. قال بعضهم: لم يَتَبَيَّن من ذلك الإشارة إلى العقائد المتعلقة بالرُّسُل والسمعيات وبيانه أن تقول: إنكم قلتم : ابتدأ بها امتثالاً للأحاديث، والامتثالُ فَرْعُ تصديق المحدّث، وإذا صَدَقَ؛ فمن جملة أخباره أنهم معصومون، مبلغون، جائز في حقهم كلُّ ما لم يُنقض، وإذا ثبت ذلك؛ استحال ضده، وكذلك السمعيات، فإنها متعلقات من قبل المحدّث اهـ. وقد يقال: من جملة إنعامه: إرسالُ الرُّسُل المؤيَّدين بالقرآن والمعجزة التي هي من جُمْلَته أيضاً؛ إذ المدار على هذا: على مُطلَق الإشارة، لا على الاستلزام العقلي الذي سلكه المحقِّي وإن كان هو الأوجه.
You have learned from this that it also contains an indication to the proofs of the creeds. Some said: It does not become clear from that the indication to the creeds related to the messengers (rusul) and the sam'iyyat (scriptural matters). And its clarification is that you say: You said: one begins with it in compliance with the hadiths, and compliance is a branch of believing the narrator (al-muhaddith). And if he is truthful, then among his reports is that they (the messengers) are infallible (ma'sumun), conveyers (muballighun), and permissible regarding them everything that does not nullify, and when that is established, its opposite is impossible; and likewise the sam'iyyat, for they are matters from the narrator. And it may be said: Among His blessings is the sending of the messengers supported by the Qur'an and the miracle (mu'jiza) which is also part of it; for the criterion is absolute indication (mutlaq al-ishara), not intellectual entailment (al-istilzam al-'aqli) which the researcher pursued — even if it is the more appropriate (awjah).
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is an argument demonstrating how the basmala contains an indirect indication to the proofs of the creeds, specifically those related to prophethood (rusul) and the sam'iyyat (matters known only through revelation). The author acknowledges an objection: some say the basmala does not clearly point to these creeds. The response is presented in two ways. First, by analyzing the reason for reciting the basmala: it is done in compliance with hadiths. Compliance presupposes belief in the truthfulness of the Prophet (the narrator). If the Prophet is truthful, then his reports about the prophets — that they are infallible, conveyers, etc. — are accepted. Once that is established, the opposite becomes impossible. Similarly, the sam'iyyat are matters reported by the Prophet. So the basmala indirectly points to all of this. Second, an alternative explanation is offered: simply that sending prophets supported by miracles is part of Allah's blessings mentioned in the basmala (as in 'al-rahman al-rahim'). The author notes that the criterion here is mere indication, not strict intellectual entailment, though the latter is more rigorous. This shows the hermeneutical depth of the basmala as a concise phrase containing all essential creeds.

أدلة العقائد
رسل
سمعيات
امتثال
محدث
عصمة
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the basmala only mentions Allah's names and attributes, with no reference to prophethood or the afterlife.
Correction: The basmala indirectly indicates these matters through the logic of compliance with hadith (which requires trusting the Prophet's reports) and by counting the sending of prophets as part of Allah's blessings.

Checkpoint

B) It implies it through the command to begin with it in compliance with hadith, which requires believing the Prophet's reports
C) It mentions the word 'infallible' directly
D) It proves it by logical necessity

Key Takeaway
The basmala, though concise, indirectly encapsulates the entire Islamic creed, including prophethood and sam'iyyat, through the logic of compliance with hadith and the concept of divine blessings.

Benefit of Salat for Prophets
Al-Bajuri presents and resolves a debate on prophetic benefit from salat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct Islamic position that prophets benefit from the salat of believers even after death, and the theological reasoning based on their continuous ascent in perfection.

Core Idea
Prophets continually benefit from our salat, ascending in perfection forever.

This lesson addresses a subtle theological question: does the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and other prophets gain benefit from the prayers (salat) believers send upon them? While some argued that the benefit returns only to the one praying, the correct view affirms that prophets continue to ascend in perfection eternally and thus benefit. Let's examine the source passage and its commentary to understand this doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage along with its literal translation to grasp the original formulation and the main points.
Notice the concise style of the matn.
2
Identify the two opinions
Find the statement of the correct view (الصحيح) and the opposing opinion (وقيل). Understand what each claims about the benefit of salat.
The opposing view says benefit only for the one praying because perfections are already poured.
3
Understand the refutation
Read the refutation (ورد) that the Prophet continuously ascends in perfections. Notice the Quranic evidence (93:4) and its interpretation by ahl al-haqiqa.
The verse is understood to mean each later moment is better than the previous.
4
Note the timing nuance
The commentary clarifies that the difference of opinion concerns benefit after death; before death, benefit is agreed upon. Reflect on why this distinction matters.
5
Apply to other prophets
The passage explicitly extends the ruling to all prophets (كغيره من باقي الأنبياء). Recognize that our salat benefits all prophets, not just Muhammad ﷺ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصحيح أنه ينتفع بالصلاة عليه كغيره من باقي الأنبياء. وقيل: المنفعة عائدة على المصلى ليس إلا لأنه قد أُفْرغَتْ عليه الكمالات. ورد: بأنه لا يزال يترقى في الكمالات دائماً وأبداً؛ إذ ما من كمال إلا وعند الله أَكْمَلُ منه كما أُشِيرَ لذلك بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَلآخِرَةُ خَيْرٌ لَكَ مِنَ الْأُولَى﴾ بناء على ما قاله أهلُ الحقيقة من أن المعنى ولَلَّحْظَةُ المتأخرة خير لك من اللحظة المتقدمة، لكن لا ينبغي التصريح بذلك، وقد أشار بعضهم لذلك بقوله: وَصَحْحُوا بِأَنَّهُ يَنْتَفِعُ بِذِي الصَّلَاةِ شَأْنُهُ مُرْتَفِعُ تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي. (قوله: وَلِلذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ بِوَضْعِ) ظاهرُهُ أنه موضوع لهما بوضع واحد. فليحرز. (قوله: كَغَيْرِهِ مِنْ بَاقِي الْأَنْبِيَاءِ أي فإن الصحيح أنهم ينتفعون بصلاتنا عليهم، فالخلاف جارٍ فيهم أيضاً كما تُصَرِّحُ به عبارة الشَّرْقَاوِي على الهُدْهُدِي، خلافاً لما يُوهِمُهُ ظاهر المحشي والظاهرُ: أن هذا الخلاف إنما هو بعد الوفاة، أما قَبْلَها؛ فالظاهرُ أنه ينتفِعُ قولاً واحداً أخذاً من التعليل. (قوله: لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ أُفْرَغَتْ عَلَيْهِ الْكَمَالَاتُ أي: حين خروجه من الدنيا، وأما قبل ذلك؛ فكان يترقى في الكمالات تأمل. (قوله: بِأَنَّهُ يَنْتَفِعُ) لعل الباء زائدة، أو ضَمَّنَ (صححوا) معنى تمشكوا مثلاً.
And the correct view is that he benefits from prayer upon him like the rest of the prophets. And it was said: The benefit returns only to the one praying, because the perfections have been poured upon him (the Prophet). And it was refuted: by that he continues to ascend in perfections forever and ever; for there is no perfection except that with Allah there is something more perfect, as indicated by His saying: 'And the Hereafter is better for you than the first' based on what the people of reality said that the meaning is 'and the later moment is better for you than the previous moment', but it is not appropriate to state that explicitly. And some alluded to that by his saying: 'And they corrected that he benefits from the one of prayer, his status is elevated.' (Reports of al-Allama Muhammad al-Anbabi). (His saying: 'and for gold and silver by one coinage') Its apparent meaning is that it is coined for them by one coinage. So let it be noted. (His saying: 'like other than him from the rest of the prophets') i.e., the correct view is that they benefit from our prayer upon them, so the difference of opinion applies to them as well, as is made clear by the expression of al-Sharqawi on al-Hudhudi, contrary to what the apparent meaning of the commentator suggests. And the apparent is that this difference is only after death; as for before it, it is apparent that he benefits by one opinion, taken from the reasoning. (His saying: 'because the perfections have been poured upon him') i.e., at the time of his departure from the world; as for before that, he was ascending in perfections. Reflect. (His saying: 'that he benefits') Perhaps the 'ba' is extra, or they have included (corrected) the meaning of 'they held fast' for example.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage resolves the debate on whether the Prophet Muhammad (and other prophets) benefit from the salat of believers. The correct view is that they do benefit, contrary to the opinion that only the one praying benefits. The refutation is based on the Prophet's continuous ascent in perfections, supported by Quran 93:4 as interpreted by the people of reality (ahl al-haqiqa) that each successive moment is better. The commentary clarifies that the benefit occurs after death, but before death it is agreed upon. It also comments on specific phrases from the text, addressing potential misunderstandings about the coinage of words and the meaning of 'benefit'.

Correction: The correct view is that prophets continue to ascend in perfections forever, so they benefit from our salat even after death.

Why Rasul Allah Instead of Nabi Allah
Al-Bajuri explains the superiority of messengership and the rhetorical reason for explicit attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author specifically used 'Rasul Allah' rather than 'Nabi Allah' and the theological and rhetorical significance behind that choice.

Core Idea
Messengership is superior to prophethood, and explicit naming amplifies honor.

Al-Bajuri addresses a subtle choice of wording in the creed. He explains why the author avoided a simpler pronoun and opted for the full phrase, linking it to a doctrinal hierarchy. This lesson unpacks the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the two main points: the superiority of risala over nubuwwa, and the rhetorical choice of explicit mention.
2
Understand the hierarchy of messengership and prophethood
Al-Bajuri states that messengership (risala) is nobler than prophethood (nubuwwa) according to the correct view. Note the dissenting opinion of al-'Izz ibn Abd al-Salam.
This is a theological distinction, not just a terminological one.
3
Examine the grammatical expectation
The context would normally call for a pronoun ('His messenger') because of a previous reference. Al-Bajuri explains why the explicit name 'Allah' is used instead.
This is a matter of balagha (rhetoric).
4
Appreciate the subtle point (nukta) of explicit mention
The explicit mention of 'Allah' serves to magnify the Prophet's status by directly attributing him to the divine name. Reflect on Al-Bajuri's exclamation: 'How noble is that addition!'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قال: على رسول الله، ولم يقل: على نبي الله؛ لأن الرسالة أشرفُ من النبوة على الصحيح، خلافاً للعِزّ بن عبد السّلام في قوله، بالعكس، وكان مقتضى الظاهر أن يقول: على رسوله؛ لأن المقام للإضمار، ولعلَّ نُكْتَةَ الْإِظْهَارِ: زيادة تفخيم شأنه بإضافته إلى اسمه تعالى الصريح، وما أشْرَفَها من إضافة.
And he only said: 'upon the Messenger of Allah' and did not say: 'upon the Prophet of Allah'; because messengership is nobler than prophethood according to the correct view, contrary to al-'Izz ibn 'Abd al-Salam who said the opposite. And the apparent requirement was that he say: 'upon His messenger', because the context calls for a pronoun. And perhaps the subtle point of making it explicit is to increase the magnifying of his status by adding him to the explicit name of Allah the Exalted. And how noble is that addition!
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage explains why the author used 'upon the Messenger of Allah' instead of 'upon the Prophet of Allah'. Al-Bajuri states that, according to the correct view, messengership (risala) is nobler than prophethood (nubuwwa), contrary to a dissenting opinion from al-'Izz ibn Abd al-Salam. The apparent grammatical expectation would have been to use a pronoun ('His messenger'), but the explicit mention of 'Allah' is deliberate. The subtle point (nukta) of making it explicit is to further honor the Prophet by directly attributing him to the explicit name of Allah. Al-Bajuri ends with an exclamation: 'How noble is that addition!'

Key Terms
الرسالة
النبوة
الإظهار
الإضمار
تفخيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The terms 'prophet' and 'messenger' are interchangeable and equal in rank.
Correction: Al-Bajuri clarifies that messengership is nobler than prophethood according to the correct view, citing a contrary opinion.

Checkpoint
Why does Al-Bajuri say the author used 'Rasul Allah' instead of 'Nabi Allah'?
A) Because prophethood is higher than messengership
B) Because messengership is higher than prophethood
C) To avoid repetition
D) Because the Prophet preferred it

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'Rasul Allah' is used to affirm the superiority of messengership over prophethood and to honor the Prophet by explicitly naming Allah.

Prophethood
beginner
4 min
Distinction between Prophet and Messenger
Sanusi discusses the relationship between nabi and rasul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different scholarly views on the relationship between the terms nabi and rasul, including synonymy and the general-specific relationship based on the scope of conveyance.

Core Idea
Nabi and rasul may be synonymous or overlapping depending on what one is commanded to convey.

Sanusi begins by addressing a theological classification: how do the terms 'prophet' (nabi) and 'messenger' (rasul) relate? Some scholars treat them as identical, while others see a partial overlap based on whether one is commanded to convey all rulings or only some. This lesson examines that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage on the relationship between nabi and rasul, then the translation. Notice the different positions mentioned.
2
Identify the positions
The passage presents two views: synonymy and a general-specific relationship. Find the criteria used to distinguish them.
3
Understand the scenarios
Work through the three cases: one who is both, one who is only a messenger, and one who is only a prophet. Note the condition of being commanded to convey.
4
Connect to caliph
Notice how the definition of caliph builds on this, but we'll cover that in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيل: إنهما مترادفان، وبعضهم يَجْعَلُ بينهما عموماً وخصوصاً من وجه بناءً على أنه يُشْتَرَطُ في النبي: أن يختص بأحكام؛ لأنهما حينئذ يجتمعان فيمن أمر بتبليغ بعض الأحكام واختص ببعضها الآخر، وينفرد الرسول فيمن أُمِرَ بتبليغ الكل، وينفرد النبي فيمن اختص بالكل. ومتى أُمِرَ بالحكم بين الناس؛ فخليفة كما قال تعالى: ﴿ يَادَاوُدُ إِنَّا جَعَلْنَكَ خَلِيفَةً فِي الْأَرْضِ ﴾ الآية.
And it was said: they are synonymous, and some of them make between them a general-specific from one aspect based on the condition that the prophet (nabi) is specified with rulings; because they then meet in one who is commanded to convey some rulings and is specialized with some others, and the messenger (rasul) is unique in one who is commanded to convey all, and the prophet is unique in one who is specialized with all. And when one is commanded to judge between people, then he is a caliph (khalifa) as the Exalted said: 'O David, indeed We have made you a caliph on the earth' — the verse.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage from Sanusi's Umm al-Barahin classifies the relationship between the terms nabi (prophet) and rasul (messenger). It begins by stating that some scholars hold them to be synonyms. Then it presents a view that they have a general-specific relationship from one aspect, based on the condition that a prophet is characterized by being given specific rulings (ahkam) to convey, whereas a messenger is commanded to convey all rulings. This results in a partial overlap: a person commanded to convey some rulings and also specialized with others is both prophet and messenger; one commanded to convey all rulings is exclusively a messenger; one specialized with all rulings (but not commanded to convey) is exclusively a prophet. The passage then adds that whoever is commanded to judge among people is a caliph, citing the Qur'anic address to David (peace be upon him) where God says He made him a caliph on earth. This connects the concept of caliphate to the authority to judge.

Key Terms
نبي
رسول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The terms nabi and rasul are completely distinct and never refer to the same person.
Correction: According to Sanusi, they can be synonymous or overlapping; a person can be both a prophet and a messenger.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes a messenger (rasul) from a prophet (nabi) when they are considered non-synonymous?
A) A messenger is commanded to convey some rulings, while a prophet conveys all.
B) A messenger is commanded to convey all rulings, while a prophet may be specialized with rulings without being commanded to convey them.
C) A messenger is a prophet who also judges among people.
D) A messenger is always a caliph.

Key Takeaway
The relationship between nabi and rasul depends on whether one is commanded to convey rulings: if commanded to convey all, one is a messenger; if given rulings without command to convey, one is a prophet; if both, one is both.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that all prophets are messengers and vice versa? How does this lesson challenge that assumption, and what does that mean for how you understand the ranks of the prophets?
?
The core of being a messenger is the command to convey. In your own life, do you feel a responsibility to convey what you know of the deen? What holds you back from acting on that command?
?
Think of a time you wrongfully mixed up two Islamic concepts because you didn't pay attention to precise definitions. How can this lesson change the way you approach learning and teaching Islamic texts?

Definition of Caliph
Sanusi defines caliph as one commanded to judge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of a caliph as one who is commanded to judge among people, based on the Qur'anic address to David.

Core Idea
A caliph is defined by the authority to judge, not merely by succession.

Sanusi briefly defines the term 'caliph' (khalifa) in the context of prophetic authority. He states that when someone is commanded to judge between people, that person is a caliph. This definition is grounded in the Qur'anic verse where Allah tells David that He has made him a caliph on earth, implying the duty to judge with justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage defining caliph and the translation.
2
Identify the definition
Notice that Sanusi defines caliph based on being commanded to judge (الحكم) between people, not on political succession.
3
Reflect on the Qur'anic proof
Consider how the verse from Surah Sad supports this definition: Allah made David a caliph and then immediately commands him to judge with truth.

Source Text

And it was said: they are synonymous, and some of them make between them a general-specific from one aspect based on the condition that the prophet (nabi) is specified with rulings; because they then meet in one who is commanded to convey some rulings and is specialized with some others, and the messenger (rasul) is unique in one who is commanded to convey all, and the prophet is unique in one who is specialized with all. And when one is commanded to judge between people, then he is a caliph (khalifa) as the Exalted said: 'O David, indeed We have made you a caliph on the earth' — the verse.
Source pages p. 51

Then it presents a view that they have a general-specific relationship from one aspect, based on the condition that a prophet is characterized by being given specific rulings (ahkam) to convey, whereas a messenger is commanded to convey all rulings. This results in a partial overlap: a person commanded to convey some rulings and also specialized with others is both prophet and messenger; one commanded to convey all rulings is exclusively a messenger; one specialized with all rulings (but not commanded to convey) is exclusively a prophet. The passage then adds that whoever is commanded to judge among people is a caliph, citing the Qur'anic address to David (peace be upon him) where God says He made him a caliph on earth. Correction: In this passage, Sanusi defines a caliph as one commanded to judge among people, rooted in the Qur'anic example of David, not necessarily a political successor.

Checkpoint

A) Being a prophet
B) Being commanded to judge between people
C) Being a messenger

Key Takeaway
A caliph is defined by the divine command to judge with justice, as exemplified by Prophet David.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The definition of a caliph includes being commanded to judge. In your daily life, who has given you the responsibility to judge? Are you fulfilling that trust with truth, or do you ignore the weight of that role?
